тАШрди рддрджреНрджрд┐рд╡рд╛’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдкреНрддрджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рддреГрддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН рдЛрдЬрд┐рд╢реНрд╡рди рдЖрд░реНрд╖рдВ рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рдореН ред рдЖрджрд┐рддрдГ рд╖рдЯреН рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГ рд╕рдкреНрддрдореНрдпрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╖рдЯреН рдЧрд╛рдпрддреНрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрддреНрд░рдпреЛрджрд╢реА рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН рдЪрддреБрд░реНрджрд╢реА рдЬрдЧрддреА рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐рд╕реНрд░рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХрд╛рдиреНрддрдВ – тАШрди рддрддреНрддреНрд░реНрдпреВрдирд╛ рд╕рдкреНрддрдореНрдпрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╖рдбреНрдЧрд╛рдпрддреНрд░реНрдпрд╢реНрдЪрддреБрд░реНрджрд╢реА рдЬрдЧрддреА ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЧрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдГ редред

Jamison Brereton

52 (493)
All Gods
R╠еji┼Ыvan Bh─Бradv─Бja
17 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh 1тАУ6, g─Бyatr─л 7тАУ12, triс╣гс╣нubh 13, jagat─л 14, triс╣гс╣нubh 15тАУ17, generally arranged in trcas ╠е
This final, seventeen-verse hymn of the short All God cycle of Maс╣Зс╕Нala VI is met rically and thematically non-unified, and probably consists of originally separate pieces later joined together. (So also Oldenberg 1888: 199тАУ200.) The first twelve verses divide into four tr╠еcas, the first two in one meter, the second two in another. The first tr╠еca (vss. 1тАУ3) inveighs against a rival sacrificer and calls on the Maruts and Soma to destroy him, in lively and imaginative terms. In style, though not in meter, it more closely resembles verses 13тАУ15 of the preceding hymn VI.51 than what follows. The second tr╠еca (vss. 4тАУ6) is more staid, but notable for calling on not only the standard deities but also on natural phenomena for aid. The remainder of the hymn is generic and somewhat repetitive, urging the gods in general to hear our calls and partake of our sacrifice. Relatively few gods are mentioned by name; there

is instead an effort to include all the gods, whatever their current or original loca tion (see esp. vss. 13, 15). After the first two tr╠еcas, the language is for the most part easy and without much character.

Jamison Brereton Notes

All Gods For the structure of the hymn, see published introduction.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI do not regard it as worthy (of the gods) of heaven, or (those) of earth, as (fit to be compared) with the sacrifice (I offer) or with these (our) sacred rites; let, then, the mighty mountains overhelm him; let the employer of Atiy─Бja be ever degraded.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

с╣Ъji┼Ыvan pronounces an imprecation upon Atiy─Бja, a rival priest

Jamison Brereton

Not by Heaven nor by Earth do I concede this, not by my sacrifice and not by these ritual labors.
Let the well-founded mountains crush him. Let the sacrificer of an
excessive sacrifice be bent double.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The instr. of ab, in two semantic sets – Heaven and Earth, sacrifice and ritual labors – apparently are the entities that the speaker swears by.

The vs., at least its 2nd hemistich, has a slangy feel – with the unusual phonology of the root тИЪubj тАШcrushтАЩ and the lexeme n├н тИЪh─Б тАШbe bent doubleтАЩ (in my rendering), found elsewhere only in a curse in the Anhangslied VII.104.10.

The agent noun yaс╣гс╣н├бr- seems like a potential candidate for the role of technical term for тАШSacrificerтАЩ, which was rejected in favor of y├бjam─Бna-.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, may the energies of that man be enfeebled; may heaven consume that impious adversary who thinks himself superior to us, and who pretends to deprecate the worship that we offer.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

That impious adversary: brahmadviс╣гam: the next verse has brahmadviс╣гe; tam ┼Ыatrum, that enemy, with reference to the word brahma, which has occurred before, religious act or praise, the enemy or obstructer of prayer or praise;

Brahmadviс╣гe = br─Бhamс╣Зa dveс╣гс╣н─Б, the hater or enemy of the br─Бhmaс╣Зa

Jamison Brereton

Whoever disdains us, Maruts, or will scorn our sacred formulation as it is being performed,
let his twisted (ways) be twisting, scorching (flames) for him. Let
Heaven blaze at him who hates the formulation.

Jamison Brereton Notes

n├нnits─Бt is an unusual formation: a subjunctive to a desiderative. It may lend immediacy to the action, which is to be taken against a formulation that is being performed (note the pres. part. kriy├бm─Бс╣Зam).

Oldenberg, Geldner, and Renou all take vс╣Ыjin─Б╠Бni as a nominalized adjective (тАЬseine Falschheiten,тАЭ etc.), modified by or identified with t├бp┼лс╣Гс╣гi (e.g., Geldner тАЬdem m├╢gen seine Falschheiten zu Feuerflammen werdenтАЭ), rather than simply as an adjective. It would be possible to tr. it adjectivally (тАЬfor him let there be twisting, scorching [flames]тАЭ). In the published translation I chose to render vс╣Ыjin─Б╠Бni both ways, as a nominalized adj.

(тАШtwisted [ways]тАЩ) and as an adj. тАШtwistingтАЩ characterizing the flames. In this way the punishment fits the crime. Note that vс╣Ыjin├б- was used twice in the preceding hymn, VI.51.2, 13.

It is unfortunately impossible to capture in Engl. the play between ├бnu тИЪman тАШconcedeтАЩ (1a) and ├бti тИЪman тАШdisdainтАЩ (2a), with the further echo of ├бti in atiy─Б╠Бj├б- (1d).

Or he who holds us in contempt, O Maruts, or seeks to blame the prayer that we are making,
May agonies of burning be his portion. May the sky scorch the man who hates devotion.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhy have they called you, Soma, the protector of pious prayer? Why (have they called you) our defender against calumny? Why do you behold us subjected to reproach? Cast your destroying weapon upon the adversary of the brahman.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Do they not (call) you, o Soma, the herdsman of the sacred
formulation? Do they not call you our protector from taunt?
Do you not see us being scorned? Hurl your scorching lance at the
hater of the formulation!

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (and to a lesser extent Renou) takes the repeated k├нm aс╣Еg├б as тАЬwhy?тАЭ But this seems more insulting to Soma than seems wise if we are urging him to strike our enemies. I take it rather as marking a series of solemn rhetorical question setting out the reasons why Soma should come to our aid.

Griffith

Why then, O Soma, do they call thee keeper of prayer? Why then our guardian from reproaches?
Why then beholdest thou how men revile us? Cast thy hot dart at him who hates devotion.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the opening dawns preserve me; may the swelling rivers preserve me; may the firm-set mountains preserve me; may the progenitors (present) at the invocation of the gods preserve me.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let the dawns help me as they are being born; let the rivers help me as they are swelling.
Let the steadfast mountains help me; let the forefathers help me at the invocation of the gods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although this vs. begins a new tс╣Ыca, it continues the series of pres.

participles that bring a vivid immediacy to the poetтАЩs bids for help: kriy├бm─Бnam (2b) тАШbeing performedтАЩ, nidy├бm─Бnam (3c) тАШbeing scornedтАЩ, and here j─Б╠Бyam─Бn─Бс╕е (4a) тАШbeing bornтАЩ, p├нnvam─Бn─Бс╕е (4b) тАШswellingтАЩ. The dhruv─Б╠Бsaс╕е тАШsteadfastтАЩ in c brings all this ongoing action to a halt, and dev├бh┼лtau breaks the series entirely – until the next vss.

Griffith

May Mornings as they spring to life, protect me, and may the Rivers as they swell preserve me.
My guardians be the firmly-seated mountains: the Fathers, when I call on Gods, defend me!

Geldner

Es sollen mir die erstehenden Morgenr├╢ten helfen, es sollen mir die angeschwollenen F├╝├Яe helfen. Es sollen mir die festen Berge helfen, es sollen mir die V├дter bei der G├╢tteranrufung helfen.

Grassmann

Mich m├╢gen die erstandnen Morgenr├╢then, Die Str├╢me mich, die schwellenden, besch├╝tzen; Die Felsen m├╢gen sch├╝tzen mich, die festen, die V├дter sch├╝tzen mich beim G├╢tteranruf.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рджрд╛рдиреАрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджрд╛ рд╡рдпрдВ рд╕реБрдордирд╕рдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо рд╢реЛрднрдирдордирд╕реНрдХрд╛ рднрд╡реЗрдо ред рдиреБрд╢рдмреНрджрдГ рд╕рдореБрдЪреНрдЪрдпреЗ ред рдЙрдЮреНрдЪрд░рдиреНрддрдореН рдЙрджреНрдпрдиреНрддрдВ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджрд╛ рдкрд╢реНрдпреЗрдо рдЪред рд╡рд╕реВрдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд╕реБрдкрддрд┐рдГ рдЙрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрдзрдирд╛рдзрд┐рдкрддрд┐рд░рдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЕрд╡рд╕рд╛ рдЕрд╕реНрдорджреАрдпреЗрди рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖рд╛ рдУрд╣рд╛рдирдГ рд╡рд╣рдиреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрдиреН рдЖрдЧрдорд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдГ рдЖрдЧрдиреНрддреГрддрдо рдПрд╡рдВрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд┐рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдГ рд╕рдиреН рддрдерд╛ рдХрд░рддреН ред рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рддрдерд╛рд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрддрдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░рд╛рдиреН рдХрд░реЛрддреБ рее рее резрек рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay we at all seasons be possessed of sound minds; may we ever behold the rising sun; such may the affluent lord of riches, (Agni), render us, ever most ready to come (at our invocation), charged with our oblation to the gods.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Might we always be of good mind; might we look now upon the sun as it rises:
so shall he arrange itтАФhe who is lauded over the gods as goods-lord of goods, as the most welcome arrival because of his help.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Another pres. part. ucc├бrantam тАШrisingтАЩ.

Geldner and Renou interpr. dev─Б╠Бn as a truncated gen. pl., which would be esp. unusual in p─Бda-initial position (p─Бda-final being at least arguably more plausible, since truncation and the adjustment of cadences in different meters are possible factors).

Oldenberg seems to take this interpr. as tantamount to a moral lapse (тАЬтАж scheint mir Verlassen des geraden WegesтАЭ). He takes it as the acc. pl. it appears to be, but construes it with ─Б╠Бgamiс╣гс╣нhaс╕е (тАЬder den G├╢ttern am besten mit Hilfe beispringtтАЭ).

Although this is syntactically possible, it is semantically unlikely: Indra, who by the evidence of the repeated and expanded phrase in 6a is clearly the subject, is most welcome to come to us; I doubt if we care whether the gods hope for his arrival or not. My own solution is somewhat dodgy: I take ├│h─Бnaс╕е as a pass. part. тАШbeing lauded asтАЩ with the venerable formulaic phrase v├бsupatir v├бs┼лn─Бm тАЬgoods-lord of goodsтАЭ as the title given by the laud (so far so good), with dev─Б╠Бn a loosely relational acc., almost an acc. of extent: тАЬ(lauded) over/across the (other) gods.тАЭ (GeldnerтАЩs and RenouтАЩs interpr. of v├бsupatir v├бs┼лn─Бm and ├│h─Бnaс╕е vary, and I will not detail them here.)

Griffith

Through all our days may we be healthy. minded, and look upon the Sun when he arises.
Grant this the Treasure-Lord of treasures, coming, observant, oftenest of Gods, with succour!

Geldner

Immerdar wollen wir guten Mutes sein, wir m├╢chten noch weiter die Sonne aufgehen sehen. Der Herr der Sch├дtze m├╢ge es so f├╝gen, der unter den G├╢ttern sich r├╝hmen darf, der am ehesten mit Hilfe Kommende zu sein.

Grassmann

Wir seien wohlgemuth zu allen Zeiten, wir m├╢gen sehn die Sonne, wenn sie aufgeht; Das wirke uns der Sch├дtzeherr der Sch├дtze, die G├╢tter fahrend, schnell mit H├╝lfe kommend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay Indra be most prompt to come nigh for our protection, and Sarasvat─л dwelling with (tributary) rivers; may Parjanya, with the plural nts, be a giver of happiness; and may Agni, worthily praised and earnestly invoked, (be to us) like a father.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Indra the most welcome arrival in the nearest nearness because of his help; Sarasvat─л swelling with the (other) rivers;
ParjanyaтАФjoy itself for us with his plants; Agni good to proclaim, good to call on, like a father.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The part. p├нnvam─Бn─Б is repeated from 4b, with a small twist of phraseology: Sarasvat─л swelling with the rivers, rather than the rivers swelling as in 4b.

The syntactic status of the various gods in bcd is unclear. Are they all separate subjects of ─Б╠Бgamiс╣гс╣нhaс╕е (so Renou)? Or should we supply other verbs? Geldner supplies тАЬseiтАЭ with cd, but keeps b with a, implicitly making Sarasvat─л another subj. of ─Б╠Бgamiс╣гс╣нhaс╕е.

Or is this just the beginning of an All God list, with no predicates required – or feeding into the next tс╣Ыca inviting the All Gods to come here?

Griffith

Most near, most oft comes Indra with protection, and she Sarasvati, who swells with rivers -
Parjanya, bringing health with herbs, and Agni, well lauded swift to listen, like a father.

Geldner

Indra kommt am ehesten und am n├дchsten mit Hilfe und Sarasvati, die durch die Fl├╝sse anschwillt. Parjanya sei uns durch die Pflanzen erlabend: Agni sei Gutes redend, leicht zu errufen wie ein Vater.

Grassmann

Recht nah herbei mit H├╝lfe eile Indra, Sarasvati, anschwellend durch die Str├╢me, Pardschanja, uns durch Kr├дuter Nahrung bringend, und Agni hold, erh├╢rend wie ein Vater.

Elizarenkova

These two tс╣Ыcas (7-9, 10-12) are in G─Бyatr─л, and the first tс╣Ыca esp. is an elementary production, with almost no tricks (though see vs. 9). One wonders whether great swaths of RV-period poetry were similarly lackluster and therefore not generally preserved.

English translation:

тАЬMay the sons of the immortal hear our praises, and be to us the givers of felicity.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Sons of the immortal: amс╣Ыtasya s┼лnavaс╕е: sons of Praj─Бpati, the Vi┼Ыvadevas; cf. Yajus. 33.77

Jamison Brereton

Let the sons of the immortal one listen to our hymns.
Let them be very merciful to us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. consists of two 3rd pl. impv. clauses, ab and c. The 2nd is entirely straightforward, and the first is until the end, where we find a hemistich-final rel.

prn. y├й, clearly coreferential with the subj. of the impv. but difficult to construe: ├║pa naс╕е s┼лn├бvo g├нraс╕е, ┼Ыс╣Ыс╣Зv├бntu amс╣Ы╠Бtasya y├й. The only grammatical way to interpr. this is as a tag nominal rel. cl. amс╣Ы╠Бtasya y├й тАЬwho (are) of the immortal one.тАЭ But this leaves the main-cl. subj. s┼лn├бvaс╕е underdefined: it is not any set of sons that we invite to hear our hymns, but only the sons of the immortal one. But tag rel. clauses generally give additional, not necessary, information about their referents in the main clause, and so such an interpr. would leave the sentence oddly unbalanced. We cannot take the whole hemistich as a rel. cl. (тАЬwhich sons of the immortal тАжтАЭ), not only because the rel. prn. would be too deep in its clause, following both subject and VP, but also because impvs. do not occur in subordinate clauses in the RV. I think weтАЩre dealing with a poet who knew about tag rel. clauses and wanted to try his hand at one, but didnтАЩt know how they work. As Geldner points out (n. 9ab), the substance of the cl. is identical to X.13.1 ┼Ыс╣Ыс╣Зv├бntu v├н┼Ыve amс╣Ы╠Бtasya putr─Б╠Бс╕е. Given these considerations, I have not attempted to render the y├й – passing in silence over a journeymanтАЩs lapse.

Jamison Brereton Notes

These two tс╣Ыcas (7-9, 10-12) are in G─Бyatr─л, and the first tс╣Ыca esp. is an elementary production, with almost no tricks (though see vs. 9). One wonders whether great swaths of RV-period poetry were similarly lackluster and therefore not generally preserved.

тАЬUniversal gods, augmenters of sacrifice, listening to praises (uttered) at due seasons, accept your appropriate milk-offering.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yuyam payas, a mixture of milk and curds, termed ─Бmikс╣г─Б: cf. tapte payasi dadhy─Бnayat vai┼Ыvadevy─Бmikс╣г─Б, when the milk is boiled he brings the curds, that is, the ─Бmikс╣г─Б, proper for the Vi┼Ыvadevaс╣г

─Аmikс╣г─Б: a mixture of boiled and coagulated milk, curd AV. x, 9, 13 TS. VS. S’Bс╣Ы

Jamison Brereton

Let all the gods, strong through truth, hearing the calls in their turns, enjoy the associated milk.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich here does assay a little figure: с╣Ыt─Б- с╣Ыt├║- across the p─Бda boundary.

The use of y├║jya- in c is not entirely clear to me. I take it to mean that the offering, the milk (p├бyaс╕е), is ritually associated with the calls (h├бvana-) the gods are hearing. Cf. VI.3.8. Geldner and Renou think that the association is between the substance and the gods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

These two tс╣Ыcas (7-9, 10-12) are in G─Бyatr─л, and the first tс╣Ыca esp. is an elementary production, with almost no tricks (though see vs. 9). One wonders whether great swaths of RV-period poetry were similarly lackluster and therefore not generally preserved.

English translation:

тАЬIndra, with the company of the Maruts, Mitra, with Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б and Aryaman, accept our praise and these our oblations.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let Indra along with his Marut-flock, let Mitra and Aryaman along with Tvaс╣гс╣нar,
enjoy the praise song and these oblations of ours.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is essentially parallel to vs. 10: various gods are to enjoy both verbal and material offerings, with the verb stem juс╣г├б- тАШenjoyтАЩ held constant. Vs. 10 has an impv. juс╣г├бnt─Бm, but our vs. an injunc. juс╣гanta. The latter may be a substitute for the impv. in a metrical situation that favors a light final syl.

07-12 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

These two tс╣Ыcas (7-9, 10-12) are in G─Бyatr─л, and the first tс╣Ыca esp. is an elementary production, with almost no tricks (though see vs. 9). One wonders whether great swaths of RV-period poetry were similarly lackluster and therefore not generally preserved.

Griffith

May Indra, with the Marut host, with Tvastar, Mitra, Aryaman,
Accept the laud and these our gifts.

Geldner

Indra mit dem Gefolge der Marut, Mitra mit Tvastri und Aryaman sollen an dem Loblied, an dessen Opferspenden von uns Gefallen finden.

Grassmann

Dies Lob und Opfer nehme an mit Tvaschtar Mitra, Arjaman und Indra mit der Marutschar.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬUniversal gods, hear this my invocation, whether you be in the firmament or in the heaven; you who (receive oblations) by the tongue of Agni, or are to be (otherwise) worshipped; seated on this sacred grass, be exhilarated (by the Soma).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

All you gods, hear this call of mineтАФyou who are in the midspace or you who are in heaven,
you who have Agni as your tongue or you who are the means of
sacrifice. Having sat on this ritual grass here, bring yourselves to
exhilaration.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The disjunctive pairing y├й agnijihv─Б╠Бut├б v─Б y├бjatr─Бс╕е is puzzling if we take the ut├б v─Б seriously. KleinтАЩs tr. (DGRV II.168-69) can stand for the standard tr.: тАЬwhich ones have Agni as their tongue or are worthy of worship.тАЭ Klein considers this an example of тАЬopposed but nonantonymous termsтАЭ giving a тАЬsubcategorization of heavenly ones.тАЭ But when so rendered there seems to be no distinction between the two groups: the general run of gods who are worthy of the sacrifice also receive those oblations through Agni – thereтАЩs no reason for a v─Б. I am therefore inclined to pay attention to the -tra instrument suffix on y├бjatr─Бс╕е: тАШthe instruments or means of sacrificeтАЩ. Such an interpr. divides the set into those who require Agni as intermediary and those who directly effect the sacrifice. Exactly who the latter might be, IтАЩm not certain – perhaps only Soma. If I am correct, y├бjatra- is used differently from yaj├▒├нya- in the next vs. But see vs. 17 where y├бjatra- does not seem to have the instrument sense.

I consider these three vss. as a tс╣Ыca. They are thematically unified, by their focus on the gods in general and (esp. vss. 13 and 15) by their classification of the gods into groups based on their location and type. On the supposed Jagat─л meter of vs. 14, which would not match its tс╣Ыca partners, see ad loc.

Griffith

Listen, All-Gods, to this mine invocation, Ye who inhabit heaven, and air’s midregions,
All ye, O Holy Ones, whose tongue is Agni, seated upon this sacred grass, be joyful.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the adorable, universal deities, and both heaven and earth, and the grandson, of the waters, hear my praise; let me not utter words to be disregarded, but let us, (brought) most nigh unto you, rejoice in the happiness (you bestow).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let all the gods deserving the sacrifice hear me; let both world-halves and the Child of the Waters hear my thought.
Let me not speak speeches to you that can be disregarded. Might we, in nearest contact with you, reach exhilaration just on your favors.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is metrically problematic. The Anukr. (also Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition) identifies it as a Jagat─л, but the vs. instead seems mostly to be aiming to be a Triс╣гс╣нubh, like the surrounding (and thematically related) vss. 13 and 15. To begin at the end, d is simply a standard Triс╣гс╣нubh p─Бda (though with uncommon break): 11 syllables with a fine cadence. The intermediate p─Бdas b and c have 12 syllables (possibly 13 in c), but a Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence, which seems more diagnostic than the syllable count. Oldenberg (ad loc. and ad I.53.10) favors an тАЬ├╝berz├дhligтАЭ interpr. for both, in other words as Triс╣гс╣нubhs with an extra syl.; see his disc. in Prol. 67. Only p─Бda a is an unproblematic Jagat─л, and even here, as Oldenberg points out (though he does not favor this analysis), it might be possible to read the final word yaj├▒├нy─Бс╕е as a disyllable, which would again produce a perfect Triс╣гс╣нubh.

13-15 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

I consider these three vss. as a tс╣Ыca. They are thematically unified, by their focus on the gods in general and (esp. vss. 13 and 15) by their classification of the gods into groups based on their location and type. On the supposed Jagat─л meter of vs. 14, which would not match its tс╣Ыca partners, see ad loc.

Griffith

May the All-Gods who claim our worship hear my thought; may the two World-halves hear it, and the Waters’ Child.
Let me not utter words that ye may disregard. Closely allied with you may we rejoice in bliss.

Geldner

Alle opferw├╝rdigen G├╢tter, beide Welten und Apam Napat sollen mein Gebet erh├╢ren. Die Worte, die ich zu euch sage, sollen nicht unbeachtet bleiben. In eurer Gunst m├╢chten wir als die N├дchststehenden frohlocken.

Grassmann

Mein Flehen sollen alle G├╢tter h├╢ren, die Welten beide und der Sohn der Wasser, Nicht m├╢gt ihr unsre Worte ├╝bersehen; mit euch vereint lasst uns im Gl├╝cke froh sein.

Elizarenkova

рдорд╣рд┐рдирдГ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрдГ рдЕрд╣рд┐рдорд╛рдпрд╛рдГред рдорд╛рдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рдоред рдЖрд╣рдиреНрддреГрдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдГ ред рдПрд╡рдВрднреВрддрд╛рдГ рдпреЗ рдХреЗ рдЪрди рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рдЬреНрдорд╛ ред рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрдирд╛рдореИрддрддреН ред рдЬреНрдорд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдВ рдЬрдЬреНрдЮрд┐рд░реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рджреБрд░реНрдмрднреВрд╡реБрдГ ред рдпреЗ рдХреЗ рдЪрди рджрд┐рд╡рдГ рджреНрдпреБрд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдЬреНрдЬрдЬреНрдЮрд┐рд░реЗ ред рдпреЗ рдХреЗ рдЪрди рдЕрдкрд╛рдВ рд╕рдзрд╕реНрдереЗ рд╕рд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ рдЬрдЬреНрдЮрд┐рд░реЗ рддреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдорд┐рд╖рдпреЗ ред рдЗрд╖реНрдпрдд рдЗрддреАрд╖рд┐рдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛рджрд┐рдГ ред рддрд╕реНрдореИ рдЪ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдореН рдЖрдпреБрдГ рдЕрдиреНрдирдВ рдЬреАрд╡рдирдВ рд╡рд╛ рдХреНрд╖рдкрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛ рд░рд╛рддреНрд░реАрдГ рдЙрд╕реНрд░рд╛рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгреНрдпрд╣рд╛рдирд┐ рдЪ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджрд╛ рдиреИрд░рдиреНрддрд░реНрдпреЗрдг рд╡рд░рд┐рд╡рд╕реНрдпрдиреНрддреБ рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреБ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay those mighty deities, having power to destroy, whether they have been manifested upon earth or in heaven, or in the abode of the waters, bestow upon us and our posterity abundant sustenance both by night and day.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Having power to destroy: ahim─Бy─Бс╕е = ─Бhantс╣Ы praj├▒─БH, having the wisdom or knowledge that kills; our posterity: asmabhyam iс╣гaye: iс╣гi is derived from iс╣г, to wish, and is explained putr─Бdi, sons and the rest, asmabhy─Бm tasmai ca, to us and to it, that is, posterity, as the object of desire.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni and Parjanya, prosper my pious acts; (accept), you who are reverently invoked, our praise at this sacrifice; one of you genitive rates food, the other posterity; grant us, therefore, food productive of descendants.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

One of you genitive rates: iс╕╖─Бm anyo janayat garbham anyaс╕е: Parjanya, by sending rain, causes the growth of corn, and Agni, as the main agent in digestion, produces the vigour necessary for procreation

Jamison Brereton

O Agni and Parjanya, help my insightful thought, our lovely praise at this call here, you who are easy to call.
The one begets the refreshing drink, the other the embryo. Confer
refreshments accompanied by offspring on us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Agni and Parjanya seem an odd couple, and this dual dvandva is found only here. But recall that the two appear together earlier in the hymn, in vs. 6 (with Indra and Sarasvat─л), and in fact Parjanya is oddly well represented in this set of All God hymns; cf. the dual dvandva parj├бny─Б-v─Б╠Бt─Б in VI.49.6, 50.12. In our vs. the two are given a division of labor, conveyed by the тАЬthe one тАж the otherтАЭ construction of c (├нс╕╖─Бm any├│ jan├бyad g├бrbham any├бс╕е), but curiously which god is responsible for which begetting is unclear enough to have produced entirely opposite interpretations.

In his n. 16c Geldner, who does not commit himself in his tr., cites S─Бyaс╣Зa. at length, who thinks that Parjanya produces the ├нс╕╖─Б-, while Agni produces the g├бrbha-. Renou the exact oppposite: тАЬQue lтАЩun [Agni] engendre lтАЩoblation-liquide, lтАЩautre [Parjanya] le germe.тАЭ Although I think Renou is more likely correct, the analysis is by no means certain. Note, on the one hand, nearby VI.50.12 parj├бny─Б-v─Б╠Бt─Б pipyat─Бm ├нс╣гaс╣Г naс╕е тАЬLet Parjanya and V─Бta swell refreshments for us,тАЭ which supports S─Бyaс╣Зa.тАЩs interpr. On the other, Parjanya is more regularly associated with r├йtas- тАШsemenтАЩ, and one passage in one of the three hymns dedicated to him, V.83.1, is esp. telling: r├йto dadh─Бti ├│с╣гadh─лс╣гu g├бrbham тАЬHe deposits his semen as embryo in the plants,тАЭ with the g├бrbhafound here. The ambiguity is probably meant.

As Geldner points out, the two products are reconciled in the last p─Бda, where both gods are urged jointly to give us тАЬrefreshments accompanied by offspringтАЭ (praj─Б╠Бvat─лr ├нс╣гaс╕е), with praj─Б- standing in for g├бrbha- and ├нс╣г- for ├нс╕╖─Б- from p─Бda c.

Griffith

At this my call, O Agni and Parjanya, help, swift to hear, my thought and our laudation.
One generates holy food, the other offspring, so grant us food enough with store of children.

Geldner

Agni und Parjanya beg├╝nstigt mein Gedicht, unser Loblied bei dieser Anrufung, ihr leicht zu Errufende! Der eine erzeuget den Speisesegen, der andere den Keim. Gew├дhret uns Speisegen├╝sse, die Kinder im Gefolge haben!

Grassmann

Agni, Pardschanja, mein Gebet beg├╝nstigt, bei diesem Anruf unser Lied erh├╢rend, Den Regen schuf der eine, Frucht der andre, ihr beide schenkt uns kinderreiche Labung.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the sacred grass is strewn, when the fire is kindled, and when I worship (you) with a hymn, and with profound veneration, then, adorable universal gods, rejoice in the oblation (offered) today at this our sacrifice.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When the ritual grass has been strewn, when the fire is being kindled, I seek to entice (them) here with a hymn, with great reverence.
At this rite of ours here today, all you gods deserving the sacrifice,
bring yourselves to exhilaration on the oblation.

Jamison Brereton Notes

A typical final vs. summarizing the ritual. For yajatr─Бс╕е see comm. ad vs. 13.

Griffith

When holy grass is strewn and fire enkindled, with hymn and lowly homage I invite you.
All-Gods, to day in this our great assembly rejoice, ye Holy, in the gifts we offer.

Geldner

Bei ausgelegtem Barhis, bei entz├╝ndetem Feuer lade ich unter Verneigung mit gro├Яem Liede ein: Ihr G├╢tter alle erg├╢tzet euch heut an dieser Weisheitsrede, an dem Opfer, ihr Opferw├╝rdige!

Grassmann

Da Gras gestreut ist und entflammt das Feuer, so lad’ ich euch mit hohem Lied in Demuth Zu diesem Feste heute, o verehrte, ihr G├╢tter alle, an dem Trank berauscht euch.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ ! рдпрдереЗрдиреНрдзрдиреИрдГ рдкреНрд░рджреАрдкреНрддреЗрд╜рдЧреНрдиреМ рд╡реЗрджрдордиреНрддреНрд░реИрдГ рд╕реБрдЧрдиреНрдзреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдпреБрдХреНрддрдВ рд╣реБрддрдВ рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рдЬрдЧрддреН рд╕реБрдЦрдпрддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рд╕реБрдкрд╛рддреНрд░реЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рд░реБрдкреНрддрд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдЬрдЧрджрд╛рдирдиреНрджрдпрддреАрддрд┐ реерезренрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрджреЗрд╡рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд┐рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╖реЛрдбрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рд╣реЗ рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреЛ ! рдЬрд╕рд╛ рдЗрдВрдзрдирд╛рдВрдиреА рдкреНрд░рджреАрдкреНрдд рдЭрд╛рд▓реЗрд▓реНрдпрд╛ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреАрдд рд╡реЗрджрдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдиреЗ рд╣реЛрдп рдХреЗрд▓реЗрд▓рд╛ рд╕реБрдЧрдВрдзрд┐рдд рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрде рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рдЬрдЧрд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╕реБрдЦреА рдХрд░рддреЛ рддрд╢реА рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВрдиреА рд╕реБрдкрд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд░реБрдЬрд╡рд┐рд▓реЗрд▓реА рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рдЬрдЧрд╛рд▓рд╛ рдЖрдирдВрджрд┐рдд рдХрд░рддреЗ. рее резрен рее
